Peng Dehuai Flees from Hunan to Jiangxi 65

The whereabouts of Peng's bandits after withdrawing from Pingjiang

Occupied Xiushui County on the 16th

Nanchang Correspondence: Xiushui in northern Jiangxi borders Tongcheng in Hubei and Pingjiang in Hunan. Located at the intersection of three provinces, bandits can easily be confused. Therefore, the county has suffered from the ravages of Peng (Dehuai) and Huang (Gonglue), the rebel soldiers of Pingjiang, since the year before last, and the poison is unbearable. Although Peng and Huang have drifted into western and southern Jiangxi, the small groups of communist remnants have not been eliminated. It is verified that Peng's bandits are the Fifth Army of the Communist bandits, with thousands of people and more than a thousand guns. Last month, they invaded Yichun, Shanggao, Gaoan, and Lianhua in western Jiangxi. Later, they were encircled and suppressed by Deng Ying's two brigades, Zhu Yaohua's brigade, and Chen Lei's regiment, and the bandits were defeated. The above counties were recovered. Peng's bandits actually fled from Tonggu and Wanzai to Pingliu in Hunan,联合the local communists on the border of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi to capture Pingjiang. He Jian sent five regiments to encircle and suppress them and telegraphed Jiangxi Province to send troops to block them. Peng's bandits saw that the large troops of the Hunan Army had arrived and withdrew from Pingjiang on the 9th, claiming to attack Yuezhou, but secretly moved towards the border of Jiangxi. Because the garrison in this province is sparse, Xiu (Shui), Tong (Gu), and Wan (Zai) are all very tight. Also, because the defense line is too long, it is difficult to block them. According to a telegram from Wuning, Xiushui County was captured by Peng's bandits again on the 16th. The county magistrate and the chief of public security are missing. Countless county residents were brutally killed. The order in the city is extremely chaotic. Farmers in the four townships are fleeing in droves. Wuning, which borders the county, is also very panicked. After County Magistrate Liu Bingkun learned of the above news, he sent a telegram to the provincial government and the Bandit Suppression Headquarters for help, requesting that troops be sent to rescue them as soon as possible. It is heard that the authorities have telegraphed Zhu's brigade and Chen's regiment to quickly encircle and suppress them. (18th)

Communist Party Organization Cracked in Gulangyu 66

Xiamen Correspondence: Although the Communist Party in Xiamen does not engage in violent acts, distributing leaflets and shouting slogans are common. According to investigations, the authorities have long known that the Fujian Provincial Party Department of the Communist Party is located in Xiamen and that it is located in Gulangyu, but they have been unable to find its location. On the night of the 13th and the 14th, three important Communist Party organizations were cracked in Gulangyu, and it was learned that they were part of the Provincial Party Department.

Previously, a detective from the Gulangyu Public Works Bureau discovered that the residents on the third floor of No. 21, Anzaijiao, were behaving suspiciously. They heard the sound of machinery at night and secretly investigated. At 11:00 PM on the night of the 13th, the Public Works Bureau patrol chief, Bassi, led detectives to surround and search No. 21. Two workers escaped upon hearing the news. Eight lead type trays, a bundle of lead bars, three boxes of black and red ink paste, a printing press, a German printing machine, and a package of important drafts awaiting printing were seized. Later, a worker from the Japanese Boai Hospital at Xizai Wharf was often seen going to No. 21. Upon investigation, his residence was in a small house behind the Boai Hospital garden. The smell of ink used for printing could be smelled from outside. At 10:00 AM on the 14th, Patrol Chief Bassi led detectives, together with the police from the Japanese Consulate, to search the small house in Boai Hospital. They found two large rattan boxes and a large wooden box. The rattan boxes contained many printed leaflets, magazines, books, and other items. The wooden box contained a complete set of new-style lithographic printing machines and lithographic plates newly purchased from the Kanō Store in Tokyo, Japan. The Party took the worker to the bureau for questioning. According to his供, his name is Zeng Shuiyu, from Huian, 25 years old. The rattan and wooden boxes were deposited by Su Wenying. Su lives in Gangzihou. At 11:00, Bassi arrested Su Wenying, Su Nengquan, and Su Baoquan in a Chinese枋皮style small house without a house number in Gangzihou and seized drafts that were being edited and waiting to be printed and a large package of documents from the Fujian Provincial Party Department of the Communist Party. According to them, they are all from Huian. Wenying is 24 years old and a graduate of Jimei Normal School. As a result of this crackdown, it is known that Anzaijiao has a printing department, Boai Hospital is a distribution department, and Gangzihou is an editing department, which is also part of the Communist Party Provincial Party Department. Their plan was to separate the three places, and if one place was cracked, the others would not know. This time, the three places were cracked consecutively, which was probably unexpected by the Communist Party.

After the Public Works Bureau cracked the three places and questioned them, it informed the Xiamen Public Security Bureau of the seriousness of the case by telegram. At 2:00 PM that afternoon, the Public Security Bureau sent detectives to Gulangyu to review the physical evidence together with the Co-Trial Court. At 4:20, they escorted Zeng and Su and the other four people, as well as the seized items, back to Xiamen. They have now been sent to the military law office of the garrison headquarters for interrogation. (16th)

No Results from Meeting on Eastern Railway Electrical Rights 67

First Establish a Special Committee to Study the Proposal

Chinese Proposal Contents and Russian Response

Harbin dispatch on the 12th: The Eastern Railway electrical rights issue, which has been in dispute for months, was discussed at a meeting held on the 2nd of this month at the office of the Eastern Railway Director-General. Because neither side had prepared their proposals, the meeting, though called, did not involve substantive discussion. It was only decided to establish a special committee to exchange and review proposals, and that Chinese, Russian, and English would be the languages used during the meetings, with English as the primary language. Furthermore, the meeting was divided into two stages: the first to discuss telegraphs, and the second to discuss telephones. On May 6th, the Chinese side presented a general outline of the meeting, with ten detailed items for discussion on telegraphs. On May 8th, the Russian side refuted the ten detailed items one by one, particularly objecting to items three, six, and ten. On May 9th, a meeting was held at the Railway Bureau, with all members from both sides attending. The meeting started at 1:15 PM and adjourned around 4 PM. The Chinese and Russian members spoke extensively. The Russian side's opinions can be summarized as follows: the electrical rights meeting must be based on the resolution of the Eastern Railway Board of Directors on April 30th, expanding on its eight-point outline for study. The Chinese telecommunications authorities should not propose separate items for resolution at the meeting. The third item, regarding the Eastern Railway's introduction to the Soviet Union to establish an international telegraph contract, was deemed beyond the authority of the Eastern Railway and Soviet representatives, and the suggestion was rejected. The tenth item, regarding the ability to inspect telecommunications at any time, was completely rejected. The main points of the Chinese members' statements were that the Eastern Railway is a joint Sino-Russian business organization, and this meeting is between the Northeast Transportation Committee and the Eastern Railway; the opinions and resolutions of the Eastern Railway Board of Directors cannot be effective for the Transportation Committee. The third item of the Transportation Committee's detailed telegraph meeting points aims to correct the old contract's (dated November 22, 1922) Eastern Railway and Soviet Union joint-line telegraph methods, simply shifting to a direct relationship between China and the Soviet Union. The old contract should be abolished as soon as possible, and all payment methods for joint lines should be added to the new contract. However, after several hours of debate, no resolution was reached. Finally, both sides agreed to establish a special committee to first discuss the Chinese proposal and the Russian opinions. The proposals decided by the special committee would be reported by both sides to their respective chairmen. If the chairmen had no objections, then formal meetings would begin. The special committee members appointed that day were: Jiang Yi (chairman), Huang Junke, and Li Jinsong for the Chinese side; and Merkulov (chairman), Shi Xuan, and Gubarov for the Russian side. They held two meetings on the 10th and 12th. Due to intense disputes over the proposals, no results have been achieved as of today. Today, it was decided that meetings would be held every Monday, Wednesday, and Friday, with the remaining days for preparation. This is the current situation of the telegraph portion of the meeting. It is unknown how the disputes will unfold during the telephone discussions in the future. The Chinese proposal and the Russian response are recorded as follows:

Chinese Proposal (A): Outline of Proposals for the Meeting on Telegraph, Telephone, and Long-Distance Telephone Matters along the Eastern Railway Line between the Northeast Transportation Committee and the Eastern Railway: (1) Sino-Soviet international telegrams should be entirely dispatched via Chinese lines, connecting with the Soviet Union at the border, and a separate contract should be signed with the Soviet Union's Postal and Telecommunications Committee. (2) The Railway Bureau should immediately cease accepting and dispatching commercial telegrams and telephone calls, including long-distance calls, at all locations along the Eastern Railway line where China has already established or plans to establish offices. (3) In locations along the Eastern Railway line where China has not yet established offices, the Railway Bureau should continue to accept telegrams, telephone calls, and long-distance calls on behalf of China, and a joint-line contract should be established. (4) China should have the right to inspect telegrams sent out of the country at any time and place. (5) Both sides should declare the abolition of the contract of November 22, 1922. The details of the above items should be discussed by the special committee at any time, and then decided by the general meeting. (B) Detailed Proposals for the Meeting on Telegraph Matters along the Eastern Railway Line between the Northeast Transportation Committee and the Eastern Railway Board of Directors: (1) All telegrams between the China Eastern Special Region and the Soviet Union, regardless of whether they are used by the Eastern Railway or private individuals, should be handled by the Chinese Telecommunications Bureau within Chinese territory. However, for the convenience of use, the Chinese Telecommunications Authority agrees to negotiate separate measures for railway official telegrams between the Eastern Railway and the Ussuri Railway of the Soviet Union. (2) The lines and equipment remaining after the Eastern Railway ceases accepting and dispatching commercial telegrams should be transferred or leased to the Chinese Telecommunications Authority for use at a fair price when necessary. (3) The Eastern Railway and the Soviet Union should introduce and facilitate the establishment of an international telegraph joint-line contract between the Chinese Telecommunications Authority and the Soviet Russian Telecommunications Authority. (4) The price of telegrams between the China Eastern Special Region and the Soviet Union should be determined separately by China and the Soviet Union, and the total sum of the two should be charged to the sender. (5) Telegrams between the China Eastern Special Region and the Soviet Union should be handled in accordance with the International Telegraph Convention and its operational rules. (6) The Chinese Telecommunications Authority should establish offices to handle private telegrams to and from larger stations along the Eastern Railway, as well as all international telegrams. For private telegrams to and from smaller stations, the Chinese Telecommunications Authority should entrust the Eastern Railway to handle them on its behalf. The names of the stations entrusted should be specified and notified by the Chinese Telecommunications Authority. After the railway receives these entrusted telegrams, it should transfer them to the nearest Chinese Telegraph Bureau for relay. A separate contract for railway-telegraph connection methods should be established for compliance. This contract should be handled in accordance with the regulations of the state-owned railway-telegraph connection methods stipulated by the Chinese Ministry of Communications. (7) For telegrams entrusted to the Eastern Railway for relay, the Chinese Telecommunications Authority should pay the Eastern Railway a line fee of two cents (silver dollar) per word for Chinese and foreign commercial telegrams, six cents (silver dollar) per word for urgent telegrams, and one cent (silver dollar) per word for Chinese official and news telegrams. (8) The price of private telegrams entrusted to the Eastern Railway should be determined by the Chinese Telecommunications Authority and notified to the Eastern Railway for collection. The line fee should be deducted from this price. (9) The settlement of accounts and payments for fees between the two parties should be cleared monthly by the Eastern Railway in Harbin with the agency designated by the Chinese Telecommunications Authority. The cash to be paid to each other should be paid directly before the 15th of the following month. (10) The Chinese Telecommunications Authority may send personnel to be stationed in each telegraph room of the Eastern Railway to inspect all telegrams received and sent by the Eastern Railway at any time.

Russian Response Regarding Eastern Railway Telegraph Matters, Answers to the Detailed Items of the Chinese Proposal: (1) Regarding the answer to the first item, the Board of Directors' resolution of April 18th of this year clearly instructs the Eastern Railway to hand over only the portion limited to receiving and dispatching commercial telegrams to the Chinese Telecommunications Authority for independent operation. As for the exchange of official telegrams between this railway and the various railways of the Soviet Union, it is difficult to submit it for discussion. Therefore, the method of using official telegrams between this railway and the Ussuri Railway should not be proposed for discussion between the Railway Bureau and the Chinese Telecommunications Authority. Therefore, the first item of the proposal should be amended as follows: All commercial telegrams between the Chinese Special Region and the Soviet Union, whether sent to or from the Eastern Railway, and all telegrams sent by private individuals, should be handled independently by the Chinese Telecommunications Authority within Chinese territory. (2) Regarding the answer to the second item, the Board of Directors' resolution of April 18th of this year does not stipulate that this railway may transfer the railway's telegraph lines or other railway equipment to the Chinese Telecommunications Authority for management according to the principles of purchase or lease. Moreover, the original intention of this railway to cease accepting and dispatching commercial telegrams stems from the development of business and the abundance of official telegrams, and there is no redundant portion. Therefore, the third item of the detailed proposals of the Chinese Telecommunications Authority should be deleted. Regarding such issues, the Telecommunications Authority should submit another proposal directly to the Board of Directors or this Bureau. (3) Regarding the answer to the third item, the exchange of international telegraph agreements between China and the Soviet Union is not within the scope of the duties of the Eastern Railway and Soviet Union representatives, so it should be deleted. (4) Regarding the answer to the fourth item, the Board of Directors' resolution specifies in detail that the price of telegrams between the Special Zone and the Soviet Union should not exceed 22 kopecks in gold currency per word for ordinary commercial telegrams, and 66 kopecks in gold currency per word for urgent telegrams. The amount to be obtained by each party should be allocated by a special committee organized by this railway and the Telecommunications Authority. Therefore, the fourth item is proposed to be amended as follows: The price of commercial telegrams between the Special Zone and the Soviet Union will still be charged to the sender at 22 kopecks in gold currency per word for ordinary telegrams and 66 kopecks in gold currency per word for urgent telegrams. The percentage to be allocated between the two parties will be determined by the committee. (5) Regarding the answer to the fifth item, the regulation of telegraph business methods between the Chinese Telecommunications Authority and the Soviet Union Postal and Telecommunications Committee is not within the scope of the duties of this Bureau, so the original fifth item should be deleted. (6) Regarding the answer to the sixth item, this item can be handled in accordance with the method stipulated by the Chinese Ministry of Communications for the state-owned railway-telegraph joint line, except for the part concerning the Eastern Railway's use of it. However, the phrase "If the aforementioned method is presented by the Chinese Telecommunications Authority and does not conflict with the regulations of this railway for receiving and dispatching telegrams, it may be used for reference" should be added. In addition, regarding the method for passengers and railway customers to send telegrams from the Eastern Railway stations using the railway's telegraph lines," therefore, the sixth item is proposed to be amended as follows: The Chinese Telecommunications Authority should establish offices to handle private telegrams to and from larger stations along the Eastern Railway, as well as all international telegrams. For private telegrams to and from smaller stations, the Chinese Telecommunications Authority should entrust the Eastern Railway to handle them on its behalf. The names of the stations entrusted should be specified and notified by the Chinese Telecommunications Authority. After the railway receives these entrusted telegrams, it should transfer them to the nearest Chinese Telegraph Bureau for relay. A separate contract for railway-telegraph connection methods should be established for compliance. This contract should be handled by referring to the state-owned railway-telegraph connection methods stipulated by the Chinese Ministry of Communications. However, commercial telegrams sent directly to stations within the boundaries of the Eastern Railway by customers of the Eastern Railway or their passengers at the Eastern Railway stations will be received and sent by the Eastern Railway's telegraph lines. (7) Regarding the answer to the seventh item, the amount of the line fee for telegrams relayed by the Eastern Railway must be discussed and determined in detail by a special committee. Therefore, the provisions of this item regarding the number of line fees should be deleted. Therefore, it is proposed to amend it as follows: For telegrams entrusted to the Eastern Railway for relay, the Chinese Telecommunications Authority should pay the Eastern Railway a line fee, and the amount of the line fee will be determined by the committee. (8) Regarding the answer to the eighth item, it should be clearly stated that the Chinese Telecommunications Authority can only stipulate the price of commercial telegrams within the Special Zone and international telegrams excluding the Soviet Union. Because the price of Soviet telegrams has already been stipulated and cannot be changed by the order of the Chinese Telecommunications Authority. In addition, regarding the method of settling accounts for cash commercial telegrams exchanged exclusively on the Eastern Railway's telegraph lines, this railway can only pay the Chinese Telecommunications Authority's sovereignty fee for such telegrams. Therefore, the eighth item is proposed to be amended as follows: For commercial telegrams within the Special Zone and international telegrams excluding those sent to the Soviet Union that are entrusted to the Eastern Railway for handling, the amount should be determined by the Chinese Telecommunications Authority and notified to the Eastern Railway Bureau for collection. The line fee will be deducted from this price. The amount of the sovereignty fee that should be paid to the Chinese Telecommunications Authority for commercial telegrams received and sent exclusively by the Eastern Railway will be determined by the committee. (9) Regarding the answer to the ninth item, regarding this point, the Chinese side proposed that the deadline for payment of fees by both parties should be before the 15th of the month following the settlement, which is too short. It is not possible to complete the remittance of accounts from various stations, the preparation of the balance sheet, and the completion of verification by both parties within the 15-day period. Therefore, the accounting period must be decided by the committee before it can be stipulated. Therefore, the ninth item is proposed to be amended as follows: The settlement of accounts for fees between the two parties should be cleared monthly in Harbin by the Eastern Railway and the Chinese Telecommunications Authority. The cash that should be paid to each other should be paid directly within the period stipulated by the committee. (10) Regarding the answer to the tenth item, the Board of Directors resolved on April 18th of this year that the Chinese Telecommunications Authority will inspect the telegrams transferred by the railway's telegraph lines in the future. Therefore, the Chinese Telecommunications Authority should not stipulate a method of stationing personnel in the bureau for inspection at any time. Therefore, the original tenth item should be deleted.

Petition by Residents of Xinbin County, Liaoning Province 68

Shenyang dispatch: The residents of the eighth district of Xinbin County, due to their unwillingness to be placed under the jurisdiction of Qingyuan County, have repeatedly appealed without success, arousing public indignation. 1200 representatives of the district residents walked to the provincial capital to petition the provincial chairman in order to achieve their goal. The residents departed from the county and arrived in Shenyang after a journey of fourteen days, arriving in the provincial capital on the evening of the 13th. Xinbin County Magistrate Yi Wenchen had previously telegraphed the provincial government. Zang Shiyi, based on the telegram, believed that the arrival of a large number of residents from the county would pose a threat to public order and required proper care. He verbally instructed Shenyang County Magistrate Wang Jiarui on the night of the 13th to send representatives to comfort the residents and prevent disturbances. County Magistrate Wang Jiarui immediately dispatched Zhang Detang, the director of the county public security bureau, to lead a team to the vicinity of Dongling to settle them separately and provide guidance. He also ordered the residents to reside there temporarily. At dawn today, Wang Jiarui, accompanied by Bai Yuling, the captain of the public security brigade, went to offer condolences. He gathered the residents in the courtyard of the Fuling Elementary School and held talks with ten representatives, including You. The representatives stated the reasons for the boundary division and the reasons for their opposition, and requested to see the provincial chairman. The county magistrate explained earnestly, and the representatives agreed. He then gathered all the residents for a speech, saying: "I am Wang Jiarui, the county magistrate of Shenyang County. Today, I represent the provincial chairman to express my condolences to you. On the one hand, I am fulfilling my responsibility as the host to maintain order, and on the other hand, I am here to guide you. You are good people, and because of the boundary division, you have left your homes and traveled to the provincial capital to petition, which is certainly a hardship. The state establishes officials and divides governance for the well-being of the people. Xinbin and Qingyuan, dividing boundaries, whether belonging to one or the other, are all within the scope of our Liaoning province. The provincial government has no prejudice on this matter. Moreover, our Northeast has a commander-in-chief presiding over it, and there are many wise assistants, all dedicated to seeking the people's well-being. If the people have illnesses, they will surely find ways to eliminate them. I will lead your representatives to see the provincial chairman to state your grievances, and you will surely come with hardship and leave with satisfaction. Now, the Northeast is surrounded by powerful neighbors, and the people must unite, and officials and people must merge into one to resist foreign insults and maintain the survival of our nation." The residents immediately cheered the slogan "Long live our wise officials." Then, the director of the public security bureau dispatched personnel to guide them to stay nearby. More than ten representatives were selected by the residents and led by Director Zhang into the city to gather at the county government. County Magistrate Wang led them to meet with the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs and the Provincial Chairman to state their opinions. The representatives also requested that vehicles be dispatched from the Shenhai Railway to transport all the residents back to their hometown to settle down, as it is the busy farming season. It is reported that the authorities have accepted the opinions of the residents. (May 14th)

Difficulties Remain for Immigrants from Zhejiang Province 69

Shenyang dispatch: The Liaoning Provincial Government has resolved to accept immigrants from Zhejiang Province and distribute them to various counties for settlement. A batch of more than 300 refugees arrived a few days ago and landed in Yingkou. The provincial government ordered the county to settle them nearby in the farmland belonging to the Tianzhuangtai people. The Zhejiang Provincial Immigration Committee, Li Guangyu, also negotiated and reached a compromise with the Liaoning Provincial Government on the funds for purchasing agricultural tools, seeds, livestock, and building houses, agreeing to advance 30,000 yuan for all applications. The handling is still going smoothly. However, the immigrants, having lived in prosperous areas for a long time, are not accustomed to the simple life outside the Guanwai region, especially the sorghum rice, which they cannot fill their stomachs with. They requested to eat rice, or each person must be given 30 yuan in travel expenses to return to Zhejiang. Committee Member Li has contacted the provincial government several times, but there is no solution. Committee Member Li telegraphed Zhejiang for instructions today. The original telegram is as follows: "Zhu Junjian, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs of Zhejiang Province, reports on the progress of immigration. The Liaoning Provincial Government agreed to advance 30,000 yuan for building houses, purchasing agricultural tools, seeds, and livestock. However, the Zhejiang people want to eat rice, or each person must be given 30 yuan to return to Zhejiang. The Liaoning Provincial Government heard this and intends to ignore it. The local area is also afraid and dare not accept them. After several explanations and attempts to smooth things over, the blow is not small. Now the Liaoning Provincial Government wants our side to be responsible for providing food from now until autumn. How to proceed? Please telegraph instructions, Li Guangzi kowtows in the cold." (May 14th)

Imperial Prince Chichibu of Japan Arrives in Shenyang 70

Shenyang dispatch: Imperial Prince Chichibu, the younger brother of the Japanese Showa Emperor, came to tour the Eastern Provinces with the students of the National Army University to inspect the battlefields of the Russo-Japanese War. He arrived in Shenyang by special train at noon on the 13th. The Japanese Consul-General stationed in Shenyang, the Governor of Kwantung, the Commander of the Kwantung Army, the President of the South Manchuria Railway, and the military, business groups, and school students residing in Manchuria all gathered in the large square in the Naniwa-dori Fuji-cho area to welcome him. The representatives of our side who welcomed him were Wang Shuchang (Director of the Military Orders Department) and Tao Shangming (Secretary of the Border Affairs Office), dispatched by Zhang Xueliang, the Commander of the Northeast Border Defense, and Wang Jinghuan (Special Envoy for Eastern Province Negotiations), Chen Wenxue (Director of the Department of Civil Affairs), and Bai Mingzhen (Director of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau), dispatched by Zang Shiyi, the Chairman of the Provincial Government. After Imperial Prince Chichibu got off the train, he shook hands with our representatives and granted audience to Consul Morioka, Major General Suzuki, and others stationed in Shenyang. He then ascended the high platform facing south and granted audience to those standing in line to pay their respects. He also went to the VIP room south of the station and granted private audience to the Governor of Kwantung, the Acting Chief of Staff Miyake, the Consul-General Morioka, and others stationed in Shenyang. At 12:05, he boarded a specially prepared car from the South Manchuria Railway, accompanied by more than 20 cars of Japanese officials, and departed for Fengtian Shrine (the place where the bones of Japanese soldiers who died in the Russo-Japanese War were buried). As the car passed through Naniwa-dori, Imperial Prince Chichibu returned the greetings of the Japanese residents who were welcoming him. At that time, every Japanese merchant and resident along the road hung Japanese flags and arranged lanterns. When Imperial Prince Chichibu's car passed, the traffic of ordinary people was ordered to avoid it by the Japanese police. After Imperial Prince Chichibu visited the shrine, he went to the Chureito Pagoda on Chiyoda-dori to pay his respects. Ogura, the director of the South Manchuria Railway local office, explained the history and origin of this pagoda. Imperial Prince Chichibu returned to the Yamato Hotel at 12:23. The students of the National Army University who came with him got off the train and stayed at hotels such as Daisei and Daimaru. At 8:00 a.m. on the 14th, Imperial Prince Chichibu went to Wenguantun to visit the battlefields of the Russo-Japanese War, accompanied by the students of the National Army University. He returned to the residence at 11:57. At 1:00, he went to the South Manchuria Medical University for inspection. Those present included about 1,300 people from the medical university, the preparatory course, the educational vocational school, the Fengtian Middle School, the youth training center, and the youth group established by the Japanese residents in Liaoning. Athletes were selected from among the students to compete in track and field competitions for the entertainment of Imperial Prince Chichibu. At 6:00 p.m., a banquet was held at the Yamato Hotel. In addition to the important leaders of the Japanese side, those present from our side were Zhang Xueliang, Zang Shiyi, Wang Shuchang, Wang Jinghuan, Tao Shangming, Bai Mingzhen, Chen Xingya, the commander of the Gendarmerie, Zhang Huanxiang, the acting commander-in-chief of the Air Force, Rong Zhen, the director of the Military Affairs Department, Yang Zhengzhi, the adjutant of the Adjutant Office, Tan Hai, the adjutant of the Guard, Liu Duoquan, the commander of the Guard, and Li Dexin, the mayor of Shenyang, totaling thirteen people. Imperial Prince Chichibu is scheduled to go to Fushun and Gujiazi tomorrow morning at 8:00 a.m. (May 14th)

Local Communications

Fengxian 71

Opposition to the Scheduled Additional Levy: The county administrative meeting this year was held because of the insufficient funds for May and June of the 18th year. Therefore, the additional levy for the 19th year was linked to it. The entire meeting confirmed it, using the original levy of two dimes and five cents as the standard. Now, people from various districts, such as Ruan and Wu, believe that the procedures for the additional levy should first determine the purpose and then inspect the autumn harvest before it can be discussed. They believe that this move is inappropriate and have already asked the county government to postpone the re-discussion after the 18th-year final accounts have been audited. The Promulgation of the Zhenxiang Police Regulations: The Zhenxiang Police are renamed from the previous Tu Liang Bao. Its interim regulations have been revised and promulgated by the Finance Bureau. Its authority is dedicated to collecting taxes and levies from each Tu Mang Cao Lu. The funds collected should be recorded in the issued payment slips and verified monthly.

Recent News on Negotiations in the Counterfeit Drug Case: Gu Shijian, the investigation director of the Pharmaceutical Industry Association, previously discovered counterfeit drugs at the Tonghe Pharmacy in Sanguantang. He was kidnapped and imprisoned midway by thugs led by the pharmacy, who took back the drugs. The county public security bureau intervened and stopped it upon hearing the news. At that time, a disaster was avoided. However, recently, the pharmacy not only did not repent but also made false statements and threatened to withdraw from the association, causing great public outrage. According to the association's report on the truth of the investigation, it had received several reports about the pharmacy selling counterfeit drugs. Because it was afraid that there might be inaccuracies, before the investigation, it first suspended a formula and sent someone to fill it, and to show impartiality, it inspected it on the spot in the town's teahouse. It was found that the fresh gold dou opened by the prescription used Jualan and stone crabs as substitutes for Shehan stone. Other Sichuan Lian flavors were even more counterfeit, and the quantity did not meet the standards. The price was as high as one yuan and three cents, which was extremely illegal. It is now learned that the association, in addition to reporting to the county party headquarters, has convened the industry to decide to ask the county to order the closure of the pharmacy to serve as a warning.

Songjiang 72

Welcoming and Detaining Informants in the Sijing Robbery Case: Gui Zicheng and two other informants of the bandits who robbed Sijing Town have been arrested by the Shanghai Public Concession Bureau and handed over to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters for interrogation. The Sijing Town Chamber of Commerce and the Yangqi District Office learned of this and specially submitted a petition to the Songhu Garrison Headquarters requesting that they be returned to the original county for trial. The garrison headquarters approved the request. The town's chamber of commerce and district office have prepared a report to send police to Shanghai to welcome and detain them. Tai Bao A Xu Interrogates Lake Bandits in Qianwei: The original part of Tai Bao A Xu's department had four or five hundred people, divided into thirty ships. Seeing that the bandit suppression army was pursuing them vigorously, they declared the disbandment of the gang and hid in the coastal villages of Punan, waiting for an opportunity to move. Recently, according to people from Jinshanwei, the gang has gathered again, and the number of people is even greater than before. They once went out to sea, but they returned because they were not accustomed to the water and soil. They have now landed and are reportedly entrenched in the Qianjiawei area of Jinshan County, occupying Liu's Embankment Bridge and even planting flags and posting sentries. Their momentum can be seen.

Jiading 73

Buying Cattle Leads to a Fatal Case: Shen Ada, who has been a cattle dealer in Nanxiang for many years, recently went to Xiaonanxiang with a buyer to buy cattle. He argued with Lu, who owned the cattle, for a while, and they fought. Shen Ada punched Lu once, and people persuaded them to stop. Unexpectedly, Lu died the next day. His family gathered and, together with the local township police, went to Shen's place to negotiate and handed him over to Hua, the director of the Nanxiang Public Security Bureau. Because the case involved human life, he was immediately transferred to the county government. On the 14th, the investigating judge, Zhuang, and a coroner went to investigate. It is reported that the death was not entirely due to injuries.

Establishment of a Credit Cooperative: The Farmer Education Center in this county invited Ruan Zhiyuan, a standing committee member of the Fourth Cooperative Guidance Institute of Jiangsu Province, to gather villagers at the Lu family's residence in Xianbang on the 14th to give a lecture and organize a credit unlimited cooperative. A general meeting of members was immediately held to pass the articles of association. Documents have been prepared and submitted to the county government for approval.

Suzhou 74

Reconstruction of the Third Prison Branch Office, Wuxian Hengjie. The internal buildings of the Jiangsu Third Prison Branch Office are dilapidated and in poor condition. The original quota for accommodating prisoners was 200, but there are currently about 300 prisoners, which is very crowded. President Lin of the High Court, in view of this, has drafted a plan to rebuild the branch office into ten new-style prison cells. He has already appointed Secretary-General Wei Bangzhen and four others to draw up plans and engage workers for construction. Furthermore, President Lin recently drafted a plan to survey the original site of the old copper coin bureau inside Panmen Gate to build a branch prison. He has sent a letter to the provincial government for review. Once approved, construction must also be actively carried out to alleviate the overcrowding of prisoners in various prisons. A large number of counter-revolutionary prisoners were transferred to the Suzhou High Court. Yesterday (the 18th), the Tongshan County authorities transferred counter-revolutionary prisoners Wang Zongchi, Wang Zhaomeng, Li Jian, Dai Hanxia, Zhang Xiacun, Sun Yuqian, Wang Timing, Zhu Dunjie, Wang Zonggui, and female prisoner Wang Jingxiao, a total of ten people. After receiving them, the High Court sent them to the Third Branch Prison Detention Center for custody and scheduled interrogation.

The District Court Tried a Blackmail Case Involving Soil Merchants. Wu Shaowu, former Captain of the Second Squad of the Wuxian Police Force, along with Yu Jinzhou and Chen Shouzhang, Chiefs of the Water Patrol Team, extorted 1,000 yuan from soil merchant Wang Waitou. Yu and Chen were arrested and handed over to the District Court for punishment according to law. Wu Shaowu fled and is wanted by the District Court. The District Court Procuratorate scheduled a hearing for yesterday (the 19th) and summoned Wang Waitou to court for questioning. Wang did not appear in court due to fear of guilt. After the opening, the court adjourned and rescheduled the hearing, as it was still necessary to summon all parties involved. Silk Filature in Various Rural Areas Open in Succession. Although there is a new organization such as the Zaoshi market outside Xumen Gate for this year's Suzhou silk filature, the total is still two-tenths less than last year. Currently, the Xijin Bridge and other places opened on the 18th, but the arrival of goods is not crowded, and the price is around 55 yuan. If neighboring villages do not compete for purchases, it will be difficult for the cocoon price to see an improvement. Mu Du, Guangfu, Xiangshan, and other places also opened uniformly on the 19th, with the reported initial price set at 55 yuan for secondary goods. However, foreign varieties are divided into three grades, with the highest initial price set at 90 yuan, and the others priced according to the quality of the goods. Furthermore, Japanese merchants have established silk filature in Guangfu and other places to absorb fresh cocoons. The Suzhou Rural Sericulture Cooperative specially convened a meeting of villagers to not sell fresh cocoons to Japanese merchants in order to protect profit rights.

Qingjiang 75

Mother-Killing Case in Xiba Town. In Xiba Town, Third District of Huaiyin, at the western end of Changjia Pier, there is Yin Yinshi, who is sixty-eight years old and has four sons: Fengyi, Fengzhi, Fengxiang, and Fenggao. Among them, only Fengxiang lives with his mother, while the others have separated. Fengxiang has a wife named Wang, who works as a hired laborer outside. At one o'clock on the night of the 15th, Fengxiang returned home from outside and asked his mother for money. When his mother refused, Fengxiang used an iron shovel to repeatedly strike his mother's face three times, breaking her teeth and severing her tongue, causing a profuse flow of blood. The commotion alarmed tenants Zhu Kaiming and his mother Jiang, who went to investigate. Fengxiang also violently attacked them. Just then, Town Deputy He, along with duty soldiers Wang Xueli and Xu Jinyuan, arrived on patrol and apprehended Fengxiang. They reported the incident to District Chief Chen Junchen, who went to investigate. By then, Yin had died from her injuries. District Chief Chen and others, considering the case involved moral transgression, escorted Yin Fengxiang to the county government for legal action on the morning of the 16th.

May 2, 1930 (Shen Bao, Third Section) Tuesday (9)

Local Correspondence Two

Changshu 76

Request to Examine a Nine-Year-Old Murder Case. On the evening of the 17th, Jiang Baolang from Qingning Sand, Nansha District, along with witnesses Wang Guanpei and Li Qiaoming, went to the county to file a lawsuit, requesting the exhumation and re-examination of a nine-year-old murder case. Hearing Officer Shi questioned them in court. Jiang Baolang stated that in the spring of 1920, Guangji Zhi Company was building a new dike in Shazhou, and his father, Jiang Genyun, was killed. At the time, it was only known that he was injured by suppression officers. A report was filed with the county requesting an examination. Now, nine years later, the fugitive murderer Zhu returned to Sha from Shanghai to make a living. According to Wang Guanpei and Li Qiaoming, his father was not killed by a gunshot wound but was poisoned after being injured by Xu Zhong, who force-fed him opium and alcohol. He requested the exhumation and examination of the body to seek redress for the injustice. Witnesses Wang Guanpei and Li Qiaoming stated that in the spring of 1920, Jiang Genyun was injured while working on dike construction for Guangye Company. The company sent people to guard the injured. At night, Xu Zhong used opium and fire-brand, threatening to force-feed Jiang Genyun, resulting in his death. At the time, Xu Zhong secretly instructed them not to publicize the matter and promised to support them for life. Now, Xu suddenly went back on his word, so they informed the deceased's son and went to the county to request the exhumation and re-examination of the body and the arrest of the murderer. Hearing Officer Shi ordered that Xu Zhong be summoned for a joint interrogation to clarify the matter before further action. It is learned that in the spring of 1920, Guangye Company was building a dike, and hundreds of sand dwellers demanded land from the company. Suppression officers fired shots to maintain order, resulting in Jiang Genyun suffering gunshot wounds near the top of his head and the left corner of his forehead, and then dying. After reporting to the county, the former County Magistrate Yang Mengling went to Shazhou to examine the body and file a report, and separate arrest warrants were issued.

Kidnapping for Ransom and Gunshot Wound of a Patrolman. Ma Yongbin of Shajie, Dongwu District, a physician of modest means, was suddenly attacked by more than forty bandits at around 9 p.m. on the 16th. They arrived by boat at Ma's residence and rushed in with firearms, wantonly destroying belongings. Before leaving, they tied up Ma and his wife, daughter, and two apprentices and hid the kidnapped victims inside the boat. At that time, a patrol boat from the Anti-Smuggling Camp happened to be passing by. The patrolmen spotted it and ordered the boat to stop for inspection. The bandits opened fire, killing one anti-smuggling patrolman and injuring two others, surnamed Dai and Zhou. The bandit boat brazenly escaped. The next day, the anti-smuggling patrol officer sent the two injured men to Jishan Hospital for treatment and reported the incident to the Public Security Bureau, requesting assistance in the capture.

Wuxi 77

Provincial Rice and Grain Allowed to Circulate. The County Government yesterday received an order from the Department of Civil Affairs stating that the provincial government had decided to cancel the circulation permits for rice and grain within the province and had formulated measures to punish and reward the smuggling of rice and grain out of the province. The order was issued to inform and instruct compliance. County Magistrate Sun, upon receiving the order, immediately printed and distributed the measures to all subordinate agencies, instructing them to comply accordingly.

Establishment of the Municipal Engineering Office. The Wuxi Municipal Preparatory Office was ordered to be abolished. On the previous day, it transferred all matters within the office to the County Government and various bureaus for management. It is learned that after the County Construction Bureau received the Engineering Section of the Municipal Preparatory Office, Director Yao yesterday appointed officials Qin Xiangtao and Yan Zhongying to the original site of the Engineering Section of the Municipal Preparatory Office to prepare for the establishment of the Municipal Engineering Office. The organization of the office includes a Civil Engineering Section with one Chief Engineer and four clerks, responsible for tasks such as surveying and permit issuance. It officially commenced operations yesterday (the 19th).

Large Quantity of Red Pills Discovered. Wang Kunshan from Nanjing, dressed in worn-out military uniform, was found carrying thirty-five cans of red pills at 3 p.m. the day before yesterday while traveling by train from Shanghai to Changzhou for sale. However, when the train arrived at Wuxi Station, he was discovered by police officers of the Fourth Section of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway and handed over to the Railway Police Department. Yesterday, he was transferred to the county for interrogation. Wang Kunshan stated that he had previously served as a cook in the Education Corps of the Military Academy. Two months ago, he was dismissed for cause. All the red pills were entrusted to him by a friend, etc. After Zhou Jun verified the statement, he ordered that Wang be taken into custody for investigation.

Tea House Worker Attempts Suicide and is Rescued. Li Ayin (over thirty years old), a tea house worker at the Datong Hotel on Tongyun Road outside Guangfu Gate in this county, became acquainted with Li Xiubao, a female worker at a silk factory, three years ago. They rented a residence in Dingfeng Li. However, recently, Li Xiubao suddenly abandoned the old for the new, and arguments frequently arose between Li Ayin and Li Xiubao. The day before yesterday, Li Ayin was repeatedly humiliated by Li Xiubao, unable to contain his anger and harboring thoughts of ending his life. He secretly consumed one yuan worth of raw opium and several boxes of matches that night, intending to commit suicide. Yesterday morning, he rushed to Li Xiubao's home, saying, "I will die in your house." Li Xiubao, seeing his unusual complexion, knew that something had happened and immediately hired a car to send him to the Labor Hospital for treatment. It is said that his life is in considerable danger. The mistress, Li Xiubao, has been detained by the police of the Fourth Branch of the Public Security Bureau for custody, pending further investigation based on the development of Li Ayin's condition.

Jiangyin 78

Red Pill Case: Mei Shougen Arrested. News about the Zhangxiang Red Pill case has been quiet recently. A few days ago, County Magistrate Li issued an order to Police Chief Wu Bowen, limiting him to three days to summon Huang Bingzhong to the case. Yesterday (the 18th), he secretly ordered Wu Bowen to arrest Mei Shougen, who had previously worked as a foreman at the Huaming Electric Plant, because he had a shareholder relationship in the Red Pill case. He was arrested at his residence on West Avenue in the afternoon. The reason is that Hearing Officer Yang went to Wujin to move his private residence and will return to Cheng on the 21st. Mei Shougen was temporarily released on bail by the Huaming Electric Plant and Tongyuan Electrical Material Store, and he must be available for questioning at any time.

Copying House Numbers and Suspicious Behavior. A police officer from the Shiqiao Post of the Second Police Station in the South City saw someone copying house numbers and the number of men and women in Qingguo Lane and the surrounding areas at around 4 p.m. on the 18th. Suspecting that they were communicating for the reactionary side, they were taken to the station and sent to the General Bureau. After interrogation, it was found that the person's name was Zhou Shunquan, from Wangjia Lane, Zhouzhuang, and that he had mental illness. He will be transferred to the County Government for handling.

Yangzhou 79

Military Police Defend Against Lake Bandits. A major case occurred in Miaodi, 35 li south of Luzhu Town in this county, where bandits robbed three small steamboats and one civilian boat. Rumors are rampant, saying that seven bandit boats are lurking in Lvyang Lake, waiting for an opportunity to rob the Shaobo Salt Depot, etc. Yesterday (the 17th), the Shaobo Public Security Bureau specially sent a commissioner to Yangzhou to request firearms and ammunition for reinforcement. Chen Qingyuan, Camp Commander of the Huainan Four Banks Water and Land Anti-Smuggling Camp, also sent his subordinate Box Cannon Team Leader Zhang Huashan to lead the entire team to Shaobo for protection.

Gaoyou 80

Yongan Town Occupied by Bandits. Yongan Town, at the intersection of the Yangzhou, Gaoyou, and Tai counties, is a famous large town in Jiangbei. Yesterday (the 16th) at noon, hundreds of bandits suddenly arrived, looting everything and occupying the town, even raising flags. The two counties of Yangtai have reportedly sent troops to suppress them. County Magistrate Wang of this county received the news at 3 p.m. yesterday and also sent Police First Squad Leader Yang Kunyue and Police Second Squad Leader Jin Chun to lead their subordinates to join forces with the Provincial Public Security Team to suppress the bandits.

Postal Steamboat Robbed. The Youxing Steamboat of the County Construction Bureau was traveling from Gaoyou to Xinghua at 9 p.m. last night when it was suddenly encountered by dozens of bandits near Sanduo Town. They ordered the boat to stop and looted the passengers. One passenger resisted the bandits and was shot in the chest, dying instantly. Losses were estimated at over a thousand yuan.

Tongshan 81

Large Number of Suspected Communist Accomplices Transferred for Handling. Xue Xiangbin, the chief of the Second District of this county, discovered Wang Timing, who was distributing reactionary leaflets, the day before yesterday and handed him over to the county government. In addition, the Military Law Office of the Second Army Corps for Suppressing Rebellion sent Wang Zongchi, Wang Zonggui, Zhang Zhencun, Li Jian, female prisoner Wang Zhaomeng, Wang Jingxiao, and Sun Yuqian, a total of seven people, who were distributing reactionary leaflets, requesting the county to handle them. Furthermore, Wei Qiaoshi Zhao, Director of the County Public Security Bureau, discovered and apprehended two suspected Communist accomplices, Zhu Dunjie and Dai Lixia, and presented them to the county government for interrogation. County Magistrate Yang Wei, considering that the cases were related to reactionary activities and of great importance, did not dare to make decisions on his own. This morning (the 16th) at 5 a.m., he ordered the leader of the Political Police Team to escort them to the Suzhou High Court for interrogation and judgment.

Hangzhou 82

Bandit Disturbance in Xizhen. Xizhen, located about ten li from Gongbu, was suddenly disturbed by dozens of local bandits at around 5 a.m. on the 19th. There were also reports of arson. Local villagers reported to the provincial patrol team protecting the silk filature and the local self-defense corps, who went to investigate. The bandits resisted. The police station immediately reported to the Hangzhou County Government. County Magistrate Pan, upon receiving the report, requested instructions from the provincial government and dispatched a security team and a motorized patrol from the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau to surround the bandits. After about two hours, the bandits finally collapsed and fled one after another. More than twenty bandits were killed. A member of the local self-defense corps, Ding Zilong, was slashed on the head and left foot by bandits and has been sent to the Municipal Hospital. The army and police are currently searching the countryside for the fleeing bandits.

Jiashan 83

Two Kidnapped Victims Released. It was learned yesterday that the purpose of the bandits in the kidnapping of seven people in Xiadianmiao was to kidnap local tycoons surnamed Jiang. However, the Jiang family had already moved elsewhere, so they kidnapped seven kiln workers and farmers surnamed Xu. After questioning them, they released two kiln workers and told the families of the kidnapped victims to quickly prepare money for ransom.

Jiaxing 84

Discovery of Bandits in Tongxiang. It is reported that six bandit boats with over a hundred bandits were discovered near Tongxiang County, Jiaxing Prefecture, the night before last. The boats were docked on a vital waterway one li from the city, with plans to rob Tongxiang County. After receiving the report, the local authorities, considering that the troops in the city were weak, County Magistrate Ma telegraphed the Hecheng Security Team to dispatch troops to suppress the bandits. The Hecheng camp police, upon receiving the telegram, dispatched troops and hired boats to pursue and suppress the bandits.

Salt Boat Opens Fire on Anti-Smuggling Boat. Yesterday afternoon, several salt boats were discovered heading towards Puyuan in Zhaojiamiao Bridge, south of Puyuan, Jiaxing. The incident was reported to various military and police agencies in Puyuan. The garrison security team, self-defense corps, and public security bureau immediately mobilized and armed themselves. At around 4 p.m., a report was received from the garrison stationed at Yunhe Tangbei Mituojian and the silk filature that the salt boats had opened fire on anti-smuggling patrolmen. The Puyuan camp police rushed to the scene, but the salt boats had already disappeared.

Shangyu 85

The Inside Story of the Embezzlement of Compensation Funds from the May 30th Massacre. Regarding the embezzlement of compensation funds for the family of Shi Songsheng, a victim from our county in the May 30th Massacre, after years of negotiations by the Massacre Relief Association, 2,000 yuan was finally allocated from the 195,000 yuan paid by the Public Works Department last winter. At that time, Shi Wang, the mother of Songsheng, and her eldest daughter-in-law, Shi Ding, came to Shanghai and enlisted the help of their relative Hu Zongyu and Zhang Jieshou (also known as Zhang Chengyue), an employee of the Shangyu Association in Shanghai, to collect the funds in the name of the Association. Later, Shi Wang only received 300 yuan and returned to her hometown in disappointment. As a result, public opinion was in an uproar. The matter came to the attention of He Wuliang, a fellow countryman from Shangyu in Shanghai, who reported it to the Massacre Relief Association. After a thorough investigation by the Association, it was revealed that in addition to the Shangyu Association in Shanghai admitting to raising 500 yuan, Hu Zongyu deducting 124 yuan for advances, Hu's brother-in-law Wang Jinlong receiving 100 yuan, and the family receiving a net of 750 yuan, the rest was all embezzled by Zhang Jieshou. Furthermore, according to Songsheng's brother, Songquan, after the funds were received, Hu Zongyu sent an anonymous letter to the Relief Association, stating that the recipient of the funds was not a member of Songsheng's family. When the Association investigated, Zhang Jieshou had already secretly returned to his hometown. Upon hearing the news, he threatened Songquan and forced his mother and Songsheng's stepson, Zhang Fu, to publish a clarifying statement in the newspaper. Hu Zongyu was still not satisfied and directly published a statement in the Shangyu Sheng Bao, clarifying his personal situation and listing the use of the funds. Among them, the amount of money differed from the information obtained by the Massacre Relief Association during its investigation, namely that the Shangyu Association in Shanghai raised 750 yuan and the total amount received by Songsheng's family was 1,026 yuan (including 320 yuan for Songsheng's mother, including travel expenses, and 306 yuan for his stepson, Zhang Fu, including other expenses, and 400 yuan for his sister-in-law, Shi Ding). Hu Zongyu also said that if the Association could return half of the funds to the Shi family, he would be willing to return the advances he had deducted in full. Another version is that Zhang Jieshou extorted 600 yuan in his own name from the 2,000 yuan compensation funds, which led to Liu Xiaotian's advertisement apologizing to the members of the Association. Zhang had no choice but to spit out 250 yuan of the funds he had swallowed to help the Association cover up the accounts overnight in order to avoid social criticism. However, fellow countrymen in both Yu and Shanghai disliked him, and a public prosecution has recently been initiated. As for Shi's relatives, they all blamed Shi's mother, saying that the compensation funds for Songsheng's life should not have been donated to a charitable association. Furthermore, Songsheng's second brother, Peizhi, and his wife had disputes over unequal rights, leading to conflicts between mother and son, brothers, and uncle and sister-in-law, and litigation seemed inevitable.

Letter

Letter from Chen Songsheng, Danyang Relief Institute 86

I recently read a report in your newspaper's local news column, dated the 15th of this month, entitled "Danyang: Chen Case: Bandits Apprehended," which stated that the bandits in this case were Bi Xiaobing and Li Bingrong. I was greatly astonished to read this. The county magistrate of this county, Mr. Wu, has investigated my case and found that the bandits are other people and has ordered the officers to arrest them separately. It has nothing to do with Mr. Li and others. Please correct the error immediately. I am sincerely grateful. Chen Songsheng, Danyang Relief Institute, respectfully.

Overseas Chinese Donation

Nearly 10,000 Yuan in Tokyo 88

Tokyo, 19th. The Chinese Association for the Advancement of Physical Education hopes to raise 20,000 yuan from the overseas Chinese in Tokyo to cover the athletes' accommodation and food expenses in Tokyo. However, in recent years, the business of overseas Chinese has been poor. Although Minister Wang Rongbao is very enthusiastic and has already instructed consuls in various places to encourage donations from local overseas Chinese, only nearly 10,000 yuan has been raised so far. Among them, the overseas Chinese in Kobe and Osaka are the most enthusiastic. Supervisors from the Ministry of Education, managers of students studying abroad from various provinces, and the Kuomintang and other organizations have also generously donated.

Athlete Accommodation and Food 89

Athletes from Four Countries Live in One Place

Competitive Atmosphere Fills the Accommodation

Chinese Athletes Eat Shanghai and Cantonese Cuisine

Tokyo, 19th (Associated Press). The dormitory for athletes from the four countries participating in the Far Eastern Games, the Japanese Youth Hall in the outer garden of Meiji Jingu, has the national flags of China, Japan, the Philippines, and India flying high in the sky. On the 17th, Dr. Irinan led the 140 athletes from the Philippines to stay here. Soon after, the five Indian athletes, including Maxide, also arrived. At 11 a.m. on the 18th, the 120 Chinese athletes led by Zhang Boling arrived in a big way. These three countries' athletes, along with the Japanese volleyball and football athletes who were already staying in the Youth Hall, mingled with each other, and the atmosphere of international competition filled the Youth Hall. As for food, Shanghai and Cantonese cuisine is specially prepared for the Chinese athletes. In the bathrooms, athletes from various countries mingled, and Chinese, Indian, English, and other languages were spoken in different voices.

Purpose of Indian Athletes 90

To Promote Diplomatic Relations...Victory or Defeat is Not Important

(Tokyo Correspondence) The four Indian athletes participating in the Games stated to reporters that this was India's first time participating. Victory or defeat is not important, only the desire to promote mutual diplomatic relations. Due to the short time, it was regrettable that more athletes could not come. The events in which the athletes will participate are high hurdles, low hurdles, triple jump, long jump, and sprints.

Japan Sports Association Requests 91

Emperor's Attendance

(Tokyo Correspondence) The Japan Sports Association believes that the Far Eastern Games are one of the world's most important sports events and a symbol of the unity of the Eastern race, and its significance is profound. Everyone knows this. Last year, the Emperor attended the Meiji Jingu Games. This year's Far Eastern Games are even more important than before. Therefore, the Sports Association decided to send the president of the Games, Dr. Kishi Seiichi, to the palace to request the Emperor's presence to encourage the athletes from the three countries. If the Emperor agrees, the Ministry of Education will submit a formal request.

Ticket Prices for the Games 92

One Yuan Per Ticket

| Japan Sports Association Prepares to Welcome Athletes |

(Tokyo Correspondence) The Japan Sports Association held a general affairs committee meeting at the Tokyo Marunouchi Office on the evening of the 14th. All department heads and committee members were present and decided to hold an East Asian Friendship Association at the Hibiya Public Hall in Tokyo when athletes from various countries arrive, to entertain the representatives of the four countries and broadcast the exchange of events at the venue to the whole country via wireless radio. It will also invite the general representatives of the four countries to give speeches. As for the entrance tickets for the Games, they will be sold at eleven locations in Tokyo starting from the 15th. Tickets for baseball, basketball, volleyball, etc. will be one yuan each. On the day of the opening ceremony, if the venue is full, ticket sales will be stopped. Although the Meiji Jingu venue can accommodate 200,000 spectators, it is feared that it will be crowded, so there are restrictions and quotas on various entrance tickets.

Japanese Track and Field Trials 93

Special Achievements

200 Meters and Far Eastern Record

Shot Put Sets New Japanese Record

Tokyo, 19th (Den-tsu). The All-Japan Trials for the Far Eastern Games were held at the Jingu Stadium yesterday. Athletes from China, the Philippines, and India all came to watch. The competition was conducted under extreme tension. In the 200-meter final, Yoshio Takashi of the Faculty of Arts and Sciences equaled the highest record of 21.5 seconds set by Omura of Todai last year. Also, Takada Mikio of Hiroshima Youth Junior High School broke his own highest record of 13.5 meters set last year in the shot put, setting a new Japanese record of 15.68 meters. The current world record for the shot put is 15.84 meters held by Siku Zida of the United States, only 0.16 meters higher than this time.

Newly Completed Far Eastern Games Basketball Court 94

Japanese Tennis Tournament

Tokyo, 19th (Den-tsu). The Kanto Tennis Championship was held yesterday. The Yamagishi Shito team from Keio defeated the Sato Kawaji team from Waseda in the men's final. In the women's division, the Asabuki Kobayashi team defeated the Iimura Takaguchi team.

Chinese Table Tennis Team 95

Will Set Sail for the East on the Shanghai Maru Tomorrow

Honey Bee Sugar Company Hosts Banquet

The National Table Tennis Federation has selected the six players with the best results to attend the Far Eastern Games. Representatives Ma Tingliang, Guo Fuhai, and Wu Maoqing did not participate in the final due to an accident. The committee will decide on this matter today. The Honey Bee Sugar Food Company hosted a banquet for the athletes at the Park Hotel at the end of North Sichuan Road last night. Halfway through the banquet, Mr. Luo Zhengping of the company gave a speech, saying that he admired the fact that everyone was serving the country by attending as representatives and hoped that they would return triumphantly. He also hoped that they would pay attention to and investigate the industry during their spare time. Next, Mr. Yu Binqi, the secretary of the association, replied, saying that the responsibility of representing the Republic of China in the competition was not light, and they would strive to do their best to live up to the expectations of everyone. Finally, Lu Shentong expressed his gratitude. Each person received sugar, sweets, and dew from the company. It was already ten o'clock when they left the Park Hotel.

Also, all the athletes will gather at Wang Kai Photography at 1 p.m. this afternoon for a photo.

Record of the Shanghai Bank Sports Meet 98

The Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank has seen extremely prosperous business in recent years. The Shanghai branch alone has more than four locations. The total number of colleagues in the head office and various branches is approximately two to three hundred, among whom there are many young people who excel in various sports and have lively interests. Usually, they are too busy with official duties to practice, so before going to the office, they practice various sports to strengthen their bodies. Group 1: Foreign Exchange Department and Collection Department.

Group 2: Savings Deposit Department and Savings.

In the second half, the Savings Deposit Department took advantage of the victory and scored another goal by Lu Jiongde. The Savings Department failed to score any goals, resulting in a score of four to one. At 1:00 PM, the tennis preliminary rounds were held, with the Savings Deposit Department paired with the Foreign Exchange Department, the Savings Department paired with the Travel Department, and the Collection Department paired with the Inspection Department. In singles, the Foreign Exchange Department won five to seven. In doubles, the Foreign Exchange Department won two to six.

Special Feature

Notes on an Educational Inspection of Japan (1) 104

(Hu Shuyi)

The Empire of Japan is located in eastern Asia and is composed of the main islands of Japan, the Korean Peninsula, and the islands of Taiwan and the South Seas. Its total area, including invaded territories, is approximately 436 million square Japanese ri. The main islands of Japan account for a little more than one-third of the total area, so the true area of Japan is only about 15 million square Japanese ri. Since the Meiji Restoration, Japan has learned the strengths of Western material civilization and unexpectedly defeated our country in one war, and then defeated powerful Russia in another war, gaining the status of a powerful country in the East. Its rapid progress has amazed the world. Our country is separated from it by a narrow strip of water, and the neighboring relationship is very close. As the ancient saying goes, "Know yourself and know your enemy, and you will win every battle." Therefore, it is necessary to conduct in-depth research on Japan. I have heard that Japanese elementary school teachers often use our country as the only teaching material for children. What is their intention? On the other hand, some people in our country advocate friendship, while others advocate jealousy. One call elicits a hundred responses. However, in fact, few people can truly observe the subtleties of the situation in Japan. The author believes that to understand the underlying meaning of Japan's success, we should start with on-the-spot investigations. Education is the foundation of a nation, and we cannot talk about education without studying the education of that country. Elementary schools are the foundation of education at all levels, so we should pay special attention to studying the elementary education of that country. I have had this ambition for a long time, but I have been traveling abroad for many years, driven by hunger in all directions, and I have been unable to make it happen. Last month, I was pleased to learn that the Beijing Municipal Government had specially appointed Mr. Gu Yinting, the former Director of the Education Bureau, to investigate Japanese education. I then discussed the matter with him to travel together, and I was also grateful for the approval of leave from the Director of the Jiangsu Education Department. With this opportunity, I was very happy, so I prepared everything within ten days and bid farewell to my parents in my hometown, who also gladly approved of this action. In Beijing, friends and relatives held banquets for me, including Lu Jun and Lin Jun from the Finance Department, Mu Jun from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, Shao Jun and Xie Jun from the Beijing Municipal Government, Ba Jun from the Construction Committee, and all my colleagues at the school. They all gave me words of caution and encouragement, for which I am deeply ashamed. I originally planned to go to Shanghai on May 11 and take the Shanghai Maru to Japan on the 13th. On the morning of the 11th, the Beijing office of this newspaper kindly sent me to the Xiaguan Station by car. My wife, Xiufang, and my nephew, Situn, and my child, Siltu, accompanied me. Siltu, who was only three years old, jumped and cheered in the car, frequently asking his mother if he could go with me wherever I went. At that time, the train was about to depart, and the whistle urged the passengers to get off the car. So I personally sent them to the platform and onto the car, waved goodbye, and was reluctant to leave. As the ancients said, "What is most heartbreaking is parting." It is true. In the train car, I met Mr. and Mrs. Luqin and Mr. Tianhan and his brother, who were all going to Shanghai to go to Japan together. We talked about matters related to going to Japan, and the journey was not lonely. After arriving in Shanghai, I visited Mr. Yinting and learned that he had changed to a French mail ship, which was scheduled to depart at noon on the 12th. I hurriedly purchased the items that should be prepared for going to Japan and went to the China Merchants Bureau in Outer Hongkou to board the French mail ship. Mr. Chen Heting, Shen Zhongyue, Yao Zhongqing, and other gentlemen from the Beijing Municipal Education Bureau were there to see me off. At that time, it was drizzling, and the gentlemen who were seeing me off waved their hands and raised their hats three or four times, showing great kindness, for which I am deeply grateful. The name of the ship was General Metzinger, weighing 15,000 tons. The staff on the ship were all French, and I could understand the conversations in English. In the evening, I drafted a form for educational inspection, with the following format: 1. School name, 2. Nature, 3. School address, 4. Location, 5. Principal, 6. School aspect, 7. School history, 8. Number of students, 9. School buildings, including classrooms, dormitories, offices, auditoriums, playgrounds, kitchens, etc. (6 categories), 10. Expenses, including income and expenditure (2 categories), 11. Faculty and staff, including quantity, teachers, staff, salary levels, boarding and lodging, and qualifications (7 categories), 12. Grade organization, 13. Tuition fees, 14. Teaching methods, 15. Interviews with important staff. The rain stopped in the evening, and the moon came out, adding many poetic materials to the night scene at sea. The lone traveler could not help but feel nostalgic. At that time, the sea breeze was getting stronger, and the silver waves and snow waves made the ship unstable. Before I knew it, I had already entered the East China Sea. (12th, on the General Metzinger French mail ship) Important News

Boy Scouts 105

Uniforms Cannot Be Used as School Uniforms

The Municipal Training Department sends a letter to the Boy Scout Headquarters to order a ban (Central News Agency). The Training Department of the Nanjing Special City Executive Committee believes that the Boy Scout cause is very noble. However, it has recently been found that some schools in various places that have not established Boy Scout troops are using Boy Scout uniforms as school uniforms, or individual students are wearing them at will, competing to show off. If this phenomenon is not strictly investigated, it will greatly hinder the future of the Boy Scout cause. Yesterday, in accordance with Article 23, Item E of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the General Regulations of the Chinese Kuomintang Boy Scouts, it was stipulated that those who are not qualified to be Boy Scouts and those who have not been formally registered after review and approval shall not use the Boy Scout uniform. The Training Department sent a letter to the Chinese Boy Scout Headquarters to order a strict ban throughout the country in accordance with laws and regulations.

Jiangsu Compulsory Education Office 106

Will Hold Second Session of Teacher Training

The Jiangsu County Compulsory Education Preparatory Joint Office's first session of teacher training correspondence department is about to graduate. Because Jiangyin, Baoshan, Liyang, and other counties have requested that a second session be continued to create more opportunities, the office, to be cautious, sent a letter to the Jiangsu 61 County Education Bureaus to seek their opinions. The letter is as follows: "Our office believes that in order to promote compulsory education, we should pay attention to teacher training. We have accepted the entrustment of various counties to run the first session of the teacher training correspondence department, and we have compiled and printed a general overview of the situation and sent it to various counties for reference. The Jiangsu Provincial Education Department has also published a recent overview of Jiangsu education, which includes the 1,023 students in this session by county, defining it as a type of teacher training undertaking. It has been found that the students in this session are nearing graduation, and many teachers in various counties have sent letters inquiring about the procedures for continuing the session. Furthermore, the education bureaus of Jiangyin, Baoshan, Liyang, and other counties have previously reported that many students have not been able to participate. The average number of unqualified teachers in the province is still more than double the number of qualified teachers. It is unacceptable to fill positions with unqualified teachers, and it is even more difficult to dismiss them without using them. Therefore, the former Executive Yuan of Zhongda has stipulated measures for unqualified teacher training classes, ordering various counties to comply. However, it is feared that if each county handles it independently, the human resources and funding will not be sufficient. Moreover, it is difficult to temporarily transfer a large number of teachers, not only causing sudden panic in the livelihoods of the teachers, but also making it difficult to fill the original positions. Therefore, according to the principle of joint management obtained from the original admission measures and the precedent of approving Jiangning County to use correspondence courses in case of difficulties, it was unanimously agreed at the meeting of the heads of various county bureaus to organize a teacher training correspondence department. Since its implementation, it has been well-received by the education community, resulting in numerous requests to participate. To be cautious, we are again seeking the consent of various counties as to whether it is still necessary to continue running the second session. Please immediately cross out one line on the attached reply card and send it to our office by a set date so that we can actively prepare. This matter concerns teacher training, and we sincerely hope that your bureau will provide practical leadership.
