Shanghai Woman Willing to Die 168

Unwilling to Be a Rural Woman

Unable to Endure the Suffering of the Countryside

Refuses to Return After Visiting Her Parents

Cries and Makes Trouble and Attempts Suicide

Husband Comes to Visit, Wife Already Dead

Wang Qiushan, a Taoist from Pudong, who is in his sixties and lives at No. 166 Xiafei Road, French Concession, has a young daughter, Wang Xiaomei, also known as Yao Wangshi. She is 20 years old this year and was betrothed at the age of five to Yao Hongshan, the owner of the Yao Tongxing Copper Shop in Gaojia Lane, Pudong. The two got married on March 24 of this year, according to the lunar calendar. The young couple had a harmonious relationship, but Xiaomei had lived in Shanghai for a long time. Before marriage, she worked as a female hairstylist, a relaxed and comfortable job. After marriage, she could not get used to the hardship of working in the rural fields and felt lonely living in the countryside. She was often ridiculed by her aunt and younger sister-in-law. Therefore, when visiting her parents, she complained and cried. After her parents persuaded her in every possible way, she returned to her husband's house. This time, when she visited her parents on the 11th of this month, she refused to go back to her husband's house. Her parents tried to persuade her but she refused to listen. The night before, her father persuaded her again and decided to send her home yesterday, but Xiaomei refused and cried, and then had thoughts of suicide. At about 7:00 AM yesterday, she secretly swallowed 生烟 and committed suicide. At 9:00 AM, her family noticed her pale face and immediately sent her to Renji Hospital for treatment. Her husband happened to come to visit and rushed to the hospital upon hearing the news. Unfortunately, she had been poisoned too deeply and the treatment was ineffective. She died at 11:30 AM at noon. The hospital notified the police, who sent detectives to carry the body to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall corpse examination office. The criminal section reported to the French Public Court Judge Zhu Chengshen, who came to the office at 2:00 PM in the afternoon to confirm the cause of death. He sat in court and questioned the father of the deceased. He was instructed to examine the body and found that the deceased had indeed committed suicide by taking poison. He instructed the father of the deceased to prepare a coffin and collect the body.

Dies for Love of American Sailor

Sailor's News Sinks

Yu Bao Secretly Sheds Tears

Lost in Thought at the Sight

Uncontrollably Takes Poison

Later, Tang Yuanjun, a tea merchant from Guangdong, lived there and saw that Wang's prostitute was quite beautiful and was very interested in her. He redeemed her for 500 yuan and lived with her. Last year, they came to Shanghai and lived in Zhabei. Wang still did not forget her old love for Pengguan. When Tang was away, she often took out the English letter that Peng had sent her and read it. Some time ago, her apartment was about to be demolished and rebuilt, so she moved to Room 20 of the Beizhan Hotel on Jielu, near the North Railway Station. Municipal Authorities Urge Repair 171

The Road Surface on Both Sides of the Tram Tracks

The road surface on both sides of the tram tracks on the city's various roads has been in disrepair for many years and is severely damaged, which is detrimental to both traffic and appearance. The Municipal Works and Public Affairs Bureaus, in view of this, discussed four rectification methods in March: (1) A strong road base should be added in stages on both sides of the tram tracks in order to achieve lasting results. (2) The road base of the tram tracks on Minguo Road (from Xiaodongmen to Laoximen) should be rebuilt according to the Dongmen Road method. (3) The track engineering on Minguo Road should be completed by the end of September this year. (4) The road surface on both sides of all tram tracks on asphalt roads should be repaired by the end of April this year. The Huashang Electric Company was ordered to comply with these regulations. The section of the tram tracks on Minguo Road belonging to the French Concession was also instructed by the Public Affairs Bureau to order the French Electric Tram Company to build a solid road base, which was also limited to be completed by the end of September to achieve consistency. These bureaus are now investigating that the road surface on both sides of the tram tracks on asphalt roads has not been completed beyond the deadline, and the construction of a solid road base on Minguo Road should also be prepared as soon as possible. Therefore, the two tram companies, Huafa, are ordered separately to urge them to proceed and must be completed by the end of September at the latest.

British Merchant Ships 172

Selecting White Russians as Guards

Initially Recruiting Twenty-Five

The "North-China Daily News" reports that after the British government decided to withdraw the British merchant ship guards on the South China route, several shipping companies in Hong Kong decided to form their own guards. They entrusted the Shanghai Municipal Council to select White Russians. The first batch of sixty applicants underwent an examination on the 15th by Chief Inspector Fessenden at the old site of the Culty Hotel. Hong Kong Police Inspector Wolfe is currently en route to Shanghai to conduct a second test, initially selecting twenty-five men to take back to Hong Kong. They will be hired by several companies such as Jardine Matheson and Butterfield & Swire, and assigned to various ships on the Hong Kong-Shanghai and Hong Kong-Tianjin routes to prevent theft. Their uniforms will be of a specific design, and they will be armed with British government-issue Lee-Enfield rifles. Each employee will also have to sign a contract, acknowledging themselves as subjects of the British government. As for salary, team members will receive fifty yuan per month, and team leaders will receive seventy-five yuan. It is reported that the total recruitment is temporarily set at fifty men.

Songhu Reformatory Changes Name 173

Record of the Demolition of the Imperial-Bestowed Yangdian Temple 174

The Imperial-Bestowed Yangdian Temple in Pudong, scheduled to reopen the day before yesterday, was subjected to the demolition of over a hundred idols within by the local Party branch in the afternoon, in order to eradicate superstition. Only five or six statues, including Guan Yu and Yue Fei, were spared. The details are recorded below.

A Brief History of the Temple: The Imperial-Bestowed Yangdian Temple in Pudong is located approximately six li east of Lujiazui in Pudong, not far from Yangjing Town. It is an ancient temple in Pudong, housing the Great Emperor of the Eastern Peak, the Ten Kings of Hell, and various idols such as Guan Gong and Yue Fei, numbering no less than one hundred. The exact year of its construction is difficult to ascertain. It is said that it was renovated once during the Qianlong period of the Qing Dynasty. It comprises three courtyards, occupying approximately three to four mu of land, and the construction is quite grand. During the annual spring incense season, pious men and women flock to burn incense and worship. Even from various places in Puxi, many people come across the river to pray at the temple. The popularity of incense offerings over the years is unparalleled among the temples in Pudong. 175

Reasons for Sealing: The temple has been managed by the Shen family, a family of Taoist priests residing in Yangjing, with each branch of the family taking turns to manage it annually. However, since the renovation of the temple buildings during the Qianlong period, they have not undergone major repairs, leading to dilapidation. The local populace laments the vicissitudes of time. The year before last, the temple gate collapsed suddenly due to the rotten foundation, injuring several vendors. Shortly thereafter, disputes arose among the Shen family regarding management, leading to a fatal incident. After investigating various corrupt practices, the government ordered the Public Security Bureau to seal the temple and deploy several police officers to maintain a constant presence, prohibiting superstitious activities such as burning incense and worship.

Scheduled Opening: Since the temple was sealed by the authorities, two years have passed. Although some people have occasionally sneaked in to burn incense, their numbers are scarce. The once grand historical site has fallen into a state of desolation. Local officials and gentry have long had the idea of petitioning for its reopening. After several discussions, it was generally agreed that the ancient site of thousands of years should be preserved and not hastily abandoned. Therefore, they submitted a request to the municipal authorities, recommending nine members of a management committee to raise funds for reconstruction and create a new appearance. It was also decided to reopen the temple on the 18th of this month so that Buddhist believers and pilgrims from near and far could come to burn incense during the incense season.

Circumstances of Demolition: Upon learning of the reopening of the temple, the Pudong Fifth District Party branch issued a declaration vehemently opposing it, and various local public organizations also expressed various forms of opposition. On the day before yesterday, when the reopening was scheduled, the pilgrims who came to burn incense were extremely crowded, suddenly restoring the lively scene before the sealing. In the afternoon, dozens of members of the anti-superstition association organized by the Party branch also arrived and took strict measures to destroy the clay and wooden idols in the front and rear halls. The statue of the Great Emperor of the Eastern Peak in the center was particularly large, so it took many people to drag and dismantle it before it was overthrown. In this operation, more than a hundred idols, large and small, in the temple, except for five or six statues such as Guan Gong and Yue Fei at the gate, were all smashed into piles of mud. They took photos as evidence, shouted slogans, and dispersed. It is reported that the Party branch plans to convert the temple into a Sun Yat-sen Memorial Hall in the future.

Accomplices to Be Tried Together

Cao Jinbiao and others, who were arrested for forming a gang to rob and injure people, were previously released after the inland detectives were bribed. The police lawyer Wang Yaotang stated that the previously arrested defendants in this case were scheduled to be tried on the 26th, so he requested that these three also be included in the case for trial. As for the confiscated weapons, he claimed to be unaware of them. Li Wushi confessed that she had been ill at home recently, and Zhang came to visit her, but she knew nothing about the weapons. A Russian's Inept Driving 179

Indeed Kills a Chinese Child

The Public Bus Company hired White Russians as drivers due to a worker's strike. After the Chinese workers returned to work, some Russians continued to drive. These Russians had only quickly learned driving skills, so they were not very proficient, and accidents were frequent. At 2:35 PM the other day, a Russian driver from the company, Noklodav, was driving public bus No. 5818 north on North Sichuan Road when he struck a child, Luo Ahong, near Wuchang Road. The Russian driver did not stop and continued driving, causing severe injuries to the child. The police officer took the injured child to Tongren Hospital, where he died soon after. The police investigation confirmed the facts and took the child's body to the forensic office on Fielon Road. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Xu arrived at the office to conduct an autopsy. According to the child's uncle, Chen Jitian, the child's parents are in Hong Kong, and he has sent a telegram to notify them. They will arrive in Shanghai in three or four days, and he will claim the body for burial. Mr. Xu verified the statement and ordered an autopsy, which revealed that the deceased child, Luo Ahong, died from being struck by public bus No. 5818. Based on the request of the child's relative, Chen Xiaotian, to claim the body for burial pending the arrival of the child's parents, his request was approved. The defendant, the Russian Noklodav, will be detained at the police station or released on bail of one thousand yuan pending further investigation.

Dispute Over Wedding Gifts After the Death of a Fiancee 183

Gu Yonghua, a 26-year-old resident of Nanshengqiao, Longhua, makes bamboo products in Miezhu Street, Nanshi. Last year, his sister arranged for him to be engaged to Jiang Baozhen from the west of Shengqiao. The betrothal gift was 100 yuan, of which 40 yuan was paid in advance, along with a gold ring and a gold bracelet. The remaining 60 yuan was to be paid upon marriage. Gu chose a lucky date in November for the wedding and instructed his sister to inform the Jiang family. However, last month, Gu's fiancee, Baozhen, suddenly fell ill and died. Her mother prepared a coffin and informed the matchmaker, who in turn informed Gu. Gu was very distressed upon learning of this. Initially, he did not eat or drink for two days. His sister comforted him and offered to find another match. Gu said that he had spent a lot of money on banquets and other expenses for the engagement, and the local custom was to return half of the betrothal gift. He was a craftsman and could not afford this unexpected loss. Recently, a neighbor offered to arrange another match for Gu, and Gu was very happy. Therefore, he invited his sister to his house and asked her to demand the return of the betrothal gift from the Jiang family. The day before yesterday, Gu and his sister went to demand the return. However, the Jiang family said, "My daughter has been betrothed to you. Although she has not yet married, she is already your wife. She has now died from illness. We informed you, but you did not come. We had to prepare a coffin and take care of the burial. The betrothal gift and gold jewelry have all been used up and are still insufficient by dozens of yuan. Please take your wife's coffin and bury it." Gu was furious upon hearing this and insisted on demanding the return. He slammed the table and shouted and argued. The Jiang family called the neighbors, and Gu was beaten and injured. His sister helped him home. He now plans to file a lawsuit with the authorities.

Bandits Use Cars to Commit Robberies 184

Female Worker Severely Injured

Jin, a female worker in a yarn factory, was lured by bandits. Jin, also known as Jin Menggen's sister, A-San, is the wife of Wang A-Huo, a farmer from Caijia Nong, Hongqiao Road, west of Shanghai (妹年三十三歲). She is currently a forewoman in the spinning room of the Shenxin Yarn Factory in Zhoujiaqiao, earning a high monthly income. She has two sons and a daughter, all young children. The entire family relies on Jin alone for support, and their lives are barely adequate. However, Jin enjoys dressing up, which attracted the attention of bandits.

Robbed and Injured on the Road: The other day (18th) was her night shift. Jin entered the factory. Yesterday morning at 6:30 AM she left the factory to go home. While passing in front of No. 275, west end of the cross section between Hongqiao Road and Hollam Road, a car suddenly drove up (rental license No. 51, municipal license No. 30, white license plate with black characters, also said to be a test car plate). There was only the driver in the car. He was heading west from the east. The car came up very quickly. Stopping the car right in front of Jin, the driver intentionally threw the iron crank on the ground, and insisted that Jin pick it up. Jin was unable to refuse, and picked it up. Unexpectedly, the driver grabbed a gold bracelet from Jin's left wrist and a gold earring from her left ear. It was only then that Jin knew she was encountering a robbery. She grabbed the car door and refused to let go. Seeing that the situation was not good, the bandit grabbed Jin's hair, threw her out of the car, causing her to hit her head and fall to the ground. The bandit then made a U-turn and drove north. Patrolman Lu Peiyu of the Wangjialou Fifth Police Station and other stations rushed to the scene upon hearing the alarm. The bandit had already fled far away. The injured woman, Wang Jin, was sent to the Red Cross Hospital on Haig Road for treatment. It is said that the injuries were severe, and her life may be in danger.

Investigation Reveals Common Technique: After hearing the news, the reporter went to the scene of the incident for investigation. The ground was covered in blood. He pulled off a strand of hair and stuck it back on the head. According to the villagers there, Xue Huolin, the daughter of Xue Shengqi, who lives in Xiaoxuejia House behind Wangjialou, was also robbed of a gold ring worth 20 yuan by car bandits at the corner of Younigan Road when she was returning home from the Shenxin Yarn Factory at about 6:20 AM four days ago. The bandits opened to maximum speed and fled to the north. A similar robbery case has now occurred, and the responsible police station is paying close attention.

Suspicious Dung Boat 192

Li Longshou's Paper-Wrapped Firearms

Gao Guangyuan, a 35-year-old man from Yangzhou, worked as a boat watcher at the Nanshi Sanitation Station. Yesterday at around 3:00 PM, Gao was passing by the Dadatou area when he noticed a dung boat docked there for several days without anyone guarding it. While he was wondering about this, Li Longshou, a man from Songjiang, suddenly appeared, hurrying along with a paper package tucked under his arm, intending to board the boat. Gao immediately questioned Li about the origin of the dung boat, but a disagreement quickly escalated into a conflict. Inadvertently, the paper package Li was carrying fell to the ground and broke open. Gao was able to see and expose the hidden secret: inside were firearms. Gao immediately called for Li Fugeng, a policeman from the Third Watch Post in the area, who arrived and apprehended Li. Together, they seized two Browning pistols, 150 bullets, and four magazines from the paper package. As they were about to take Li to the district, another person noticed Li's arrest and immediately ran to hide on a ship docked nearby. This was observed by officers from the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol, who approached, apprehended him, and brought him along with Li to the First District Headquarters. During the preliminary interrogation by the District Chief, Li Longshou confessed that he was 40 years old and had always made a living by farming. He claimed that today, an unknown person had given him the paper package and asked him to take it to Pudong, promising him a generous reward. He insisted that he was unaware of the illegal items inside and had been foolish and greedy, leading him to be deceived. He pleaded for leniency. The other person, Wang Pujiang, 35 years old from Jiashan, claimed he did not know Li and knew nothing about the case. He said he had been startled by the police arresting someone and had fled to hide on the ship. The District Chief, considering the seriousness of the case involving privately carrying firearms, ordered that a written report be prepared and submitted to the Third Section of the Municipal Public Security Bureau for further investigation.

Aftermath of the Resolution of the Pharmaceutical Industry Dispute 193

The Labor Union Refutes the Management's Submission. The Pharmaceutical Workers' Union, seeking to refute the absurd submission from the management, submitted a document to the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Municipal Government, which stated (abbreviated title): Regarding the management's defiance of the central government's decision, requesting strict orders to comply. It is hereby reported that after the central government made its decision and the [Municipal] Council and Government jointly consulted and formulated five measures for compliance, both parties were ordered to comply. This union immediately respected the orders and fully complied with them. However, the management refused to be educated and has not complied to this day. Furthermore, yesterday (the 18th), they published an outrageous submission in the newspapers. This union, fearing that the truth would be obscured and that misunderstandings would arise among outsiders, hereby presents a reasoned refutation. The management claims that the central government's six measures are intended to alleviate the hardships of labor and management, and they deeply admire this and will comply with the orders. How, then, can they rely on their own assertions to violate the principles of the central government's decision? They illegally included a severance fee of 2,000 yuan with their submission, requesting that the Chamber of Commerce forward it to the Social Affairs Bureau. These points alone are sufficient to prove that the management's defiance and arrogance are unforgivable. Moreover, the six points presented by the management are not entirely factual, and their reasoning is absurd. It is necessary to reiterate our position to seek justice. The previous work slowdown by this union was caused by the management's excessive oppression, hiring a large number of police officers, arresting and imprisoning workers, insulting representatives of the Party, and falsely accusing them of being reactionary. All workers were filled with righteous indignation, and a decision was made by the general membership meeting to initiate a partial work slowdown. The facts are all there and cannot be concealed. As for the claim that we forcibly imposed a work slowdown without first requesting mediation in accordance with the law, we believe that the management is disregarding the authority of the [Municipal] Government and the [Municipal] Council, and that they are either ignorant or misinformed about the situation. Before this incident occurred, the [Municipal] Council repeatedly ordered the management to implement the measures within a specified period, otherwise the labor side would automatically implement them. Because the management ignored this, neither requesting a postponement nor expressing agreement, this union proceeded to implement the measures automatically after the deadline. Considering the above two points, the responsibility is clearly identifiable, yet they make an exaggerated statement, blaming others, and uttering empty rhetoric to gain sympathy. Like a fox weeping over a rabbit, how shameful is that? This is the first point that should be refuted. The central government deeply understands that the first work slowdown by the labor side was out of desperation, and therefore did not condemn it, but only deducted twelve days of wages. While the central government showed great understanding, the labor side, though dissatisfied, was still able to abide by the law and obey. The word "obedience" is evident here. Why must the management pretend to be sympathetic, offering flattering compassion? This is truly admirable. The second work slowdown occurred after mediation. Whether the responsibility should be attributed to this union or whether workers were coerced into blindly following is a matter for the trade association to consider. As the previous point has already been explained, to argue about fairness and reason is far-fetched. Initiating illegal actions must be denounced, and the intention of the central government must be respected. The question is, what if we do not consider the circumstances and reason? Furthermore, does the central government's decision only refer to wages, or are there other matters? Even if we only consider the telegram regarding wages, it clearly states, "The wages for the twelve days of the strike before the mediation decision are not paid at all. The wages for the strike after the mediation decision should be paid in full by the management." What does "half wages paid during the strike period" refer to? Did the [Municipal] Government and the [Municipal] Council not distribute the central government's telegram to us? Is the [Municipal] Government's and the [Municipal] Council's instruction No. 4150 a forgery? In short, the management's intentions are sinister, confusing and misleading, attempting to deceive the public. This is the second point that should be refuted. Regarding the allowance, in the [Municipal] Government's and the [Municipal] Council's instruction No. 35, the second item of the central government's decision states, "Workers who are found unqualified by the Mediation Committee will be given severance pay by the management as a gesture of compassion." and the second item of the consultation decision of the same number of the [Municipal] Government and the [Municipal] Council states, "The 51 people who are found unqualified by the [Municipal] Council and the Social Affairs Bureau will still be handled according to the decision of the Mediation Committee, and they will be given 20 yuan each as severance pay by the trade association." Where did the management's so-called 100 unemployed workers come from? Furthermore, is the date of the [Municipal] Government's instruction No. 589 after the central government's decision? If so, then the [Municipal] Government will also be at fault for violating the central government's decision. Furthermore, they said, "After the severance, there should be no pharmaceutical industry unemployment in Shanghai." How contradictory! The reason for unemployment is purely due to the management's oppression, unwarranted dismissal, and excessive recruitment of apprentices, who fill the positions of workers upon completion of their apprenticeship, leading to increasing unemployment. This union's placement plan is only a temporary solution. The fundamental solution has already been outlined in the submission to the central government, and the central government, understanding the hardships of the people, has ordered the [Municipal] Government and the [Municipal] Council to formulate a proper plan after the resolution of this turmoil, in order to resolve the dispute. Perhaps the management has made every effort to place the unemployed, and will never again recruit apprentices or dismiss workers. This union should naturally rejoice. However, the number of 100 people for severance is not in accordance with the facts. This is the third point that should be refuted. The substitute worker system was established by signed agreement and cannot be changed. Now, the management is using the name of severance to recklessly attempt to abolish the substitute worker system. Their devious plan is truly admirable. The management's arrangement is meticulous, and their means are highly astute. However, there is no explicit provision in the central government's decision to abolish the substitute worker system. The management's defiance of the law is evident. This is the fourth point that should be refuted. The central government has decided that the placement of unemployed workers, the number of people, and six other items should be properly handled by the [Municipal] Government and the [Municipal] Council, and the [Municipal] Government and the [Municipal] Council have jointly decided on five measures for compliance. All parties should absolutely comply. However, the management is only seeking their own benefit, openly denying and falsely using the name of human rights to slander the committees' allocation of people to various stores, undermining the agreement, violating orders, and being ignorant of the possibility of temporality and specificity. They want to use the order before the central government clearly understood the facts of this case to deceive the world, trying to cover up the new with the old. How clumsy is their scheme! With the dignity of the central government, the management actually wants to give orders and ask the central government to withdraw its decision, which is too convenient. The National Government's approval was inevitably deceived by the management. I believe that since the central government has already made a decision, the National Government should also comply. If the organization is like this, how can they use biased views to distort and fabricate the truth, and then use it as a basis for resistance? I dare to tell the responsible personnel of the management: don't dream. You must know that although money is all-powerful, it sometimes loses its effect. Justice will prevail, and it will never be destroyed. This is the fifth point that should be refuted. Feng Jinpu's arrest was a confidential order from a higher level, because Feng dared to violate the central government's decision and represented the management, going to Beijing to lobby. His reactionary crime has long been proven, and his arrest is already a lenient sentence. This union received a confidential order to assist in the arrest. Since the management has questioned this, this union should explain it, so that the outside world can understand the truth. This is the sixth point that should be refuted. Once the above six points are refuted, justice will be served. I implore the [Municipal] Government and the [Municipal] Council to discern the truth clearly and to make a fair judgment, to strictly order the management to comply within a specified period, refute the management's request, so as to conform to the intention of the central government, to meet the expectations of the public, and to alleviate the hardships of the people. Sincerely submitted, (omitted below)

The Social Affairs Bureau Returns the Severance Fee. The Shanghai Pharmaceutical Workers' Union caused a major dispute by requesting that the management place unemployed workers, which attracted the attention of the public. The Social Affairs Bureau repeatedly convened labor and management for mediation, and finally decided on a plan. The management did not agree, resulting in a work slowdown by the entire pharmaceutical industry in the city. Later, the central government decided that the management should place at least 64 unemployed workers in order to prevent the dispute from escalating. After receiving the order, the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union ordered all workers in the city to return to their original positions. However, the management delayed and failed to comply with the order. A few days ago, the Pharmaceutical Trade Association prepared 2,000 yuan in foreign currency and entrusted the Chamber of Commerce to submit it to the Social Affairs Bureau as a severance fee for unemployed workers in the industry. However, the Bureau returned it and replied to the Chamber of Commerce, stating roughly that the recruitment of displaced workers in the pharmaceutical industry only needs to be handled in accordance with the central government's plan.

The Diplomatic Value of New National Music 194

Whenever there are diplomatic events in civilized countries, they all play their national music to promote their culture. Our country flourished in the Spring and Autumn period, but it has been absent since the Tang Dynasty, which is why foreigners regard us as a country without music. The Datong Music Society in this city has recently compiled new National Music, which is grand in scale and solemn in atmosphere. Listening to it is like the harmonious sounds of phoenixes, making people yearn for the past and recall ancient culture. Recently, the members of the Society's orchestra have been working even harder, and the number of new members has been increasing. In terms of instruments, they have also newly created various instruments such as the twelve-stringed violin, danqin, and bamboo drum, which are all replicas of ancient musical instruments. They have a loud volume and beautiful sound. They attended the garden party of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs last Friday, and people from both China and the West highly praised them. At 4 PM on Tuesday afternoon, at Furguson Road and World College, they welcomed the French Minister and Dr. Ma Xuanbo, a special envoy for investigating higher education in China. There were even more people from both China and the West. Chairman Li Shizeng, who is also the executive committee member of the Society, temporarily called all the members to play five movements of the National Music. The sound of drums and applause was continuous in each movement. The French Minister and Dr. Ma, among others, examined each instrument in detail and attached great importance to this initiative for the future of our country's culture, which will add no small amount of luster.

Issue 2 (7)

The Story of World Literature (1) (5) (6) Written by John Macy, Translated by Hu Zhongchi 208

Chapter XVIII: French Poetry of the Nineteenth Century

Chapter XL: The Classical Age of German Literature

Goethe seems to us to have the illusion of deep talent and endowment, and to have the experience and sympathy for human life. These qualities will not only make him a decoration of literature, but also make him stand tall in many ways as "the teacher of life" and the model of his time. This qualification is given to him [Carlyle

In this narrative about literature, we seem to have understood that the habits of thinking and the techniques of writing are somewhat of a continuous process. There are ups and downs, flashes of inexplicable genius, and times of stagnation. Any "era" is actually not an era, because the word era seems to imply a definite beginning and end. In the story of literature, and as far as I have investigated, in any other part of the story of mankind, such a definite time is extremely rare. Events and ideas flow and blend together, so when we talk about the nineteenth century, we do not mean that an idea was born exactly on January 1, 1801. Many of the ideas of the nineteenth century can be traced back to the eighteenth century. The classical age of Germany unfolded almost equally on both sides of 1800. In this summary, we will deliberately not mention the precise dates that anyone can find in the encyclopedia. However, in order not to forget the general location, we can keep in mind that Goethe died in 1832 (the same year Scott died) and that his vigorous era of production spanned the eighteenth and nineteenth centuries. The pioneers were all in the eighteenth century.

To understand Goethe and his contemporaries, we need to trace back several years and find the things that led to that supreme master and the classical age of German literature. This is necessary.

When the Peace of Westphalia ended the Thirty Years' War in 1648, all the lands using the German language were devastated by the war, and only half of the pre-war population remained. The wars caused by the Reformation and its consequences led to the complete failure of the German artistic renaissance, and the only legacy left by German literature was folk songs. Needless to say, literature did not die out completely during the war. In the decline of civilization, the purpose of scattered writers was to keep a kind of flame burning. Naturally, such writers adopted smooth poetry, maintained the purity of language, and did not aspire to anything more than precision. This was the goal of Martin Opitz, who was considered the German Waller (Note 1) and Malherbe (Note 2) at the time. He adopted the Alexandrine verse, wrote a small essay on German poetry, and in various other ways, intended to adopt the forms and ideals of French literature of the "Great Age" (Note 3). The most original writer of that desolate era was the satirist Logau. Some of his poems are known to English readers through Longfellow's translation. We do not need to dwell on the playwright Gryphius, or on the various local societies that strive to maintain the purity of language and maintain a lively interest in literature.

Note 1: Edmund Waller was an English poet who served as a member of the Long Parliament.

Note 2: See Chapter XIX

Note 3: The era of Louis XIV's reign

During the period from the Thirty Years' War to the Seven Years' War, there were only three noteworthy figures. The catastrophe of the Thirty Years' War was described by Christopher Wangreliomermeshosheng in the thoroughly realistic novel "Simplicissimus". This story, based on the rumors of rogues, is still very readable today. We must also mention Paul Gerhard, the greatest hymn writer in Germany after Luther. Many of his hymns have been translated by John Wesley and others and are familiar everywhere where English is used.

When Leipzig was the capital of German literature in 1740, it was a kind of Mecca where Gottsched was the prophet of Barrow. In order to explain the critical aspect of the works of the great classical masters of German literature, it is necessary to pay attention to the driest, most superficial Gallic style that prevailed. Those works had their vague pioneers in Switzerland. The Swiss critics Bodmer and Breitinger left France and turned to England. They published periodicals imitating the "Spectator," especially refuting the fallacies of France with cold eloquence, and paying attention to the true solemnity of Milton. The Swiss poet Albrecht von Haller, in that poem of the Alps, imitated Thomson's "Seasons," and slightly later, the elegiac poets Salis and Matthisson imitated Gray in their poems. Some of those poems were known to English readers through Longfellow's English translation. At that time, in Germany itself, poetry was limited to imitating France.

Art World Guidelines

(1) The text is limited to news, comments, and introductions about recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature at home and abroad.

Pictures are limited to recent works by new writers at home and abroad and illustrations related to the text.

(3) Photos are limited to recent portraits and works by writers at home and abroad and various photographs related to the text.

(4) The number of words in each article should not exceed 3,000.
